       6             : 
       7             : /*
       8             :  * This code implements an incremental mark-and-sweep garbage collector, with
       9             :  * most sweeping carried out in the background on a parallel thread.
      10             :  *
      11             :  * Full vs. zone GC
      12             :  * ----------------
      13             :  *
      14             :  * The collector can collect all zones at once, or a subset. These types of
      15             :  * collection are referred to as a full GC and a zone GC respectively.
      16             :  *
      17             :  * It is possible for an incremental collection that started out as a full GC to
      18             :  * become a zone GC if new zones are created during the course of the
      19             :  * collection.
      20             :  *
      21             :  * Incremental collection
      22             :  * ----------------------
      23             :  *
      24             :  * For a collection to be carried out incrementally the following conditions
      25             :  * must be met:
      26             :  *  - the collection must be run by calling js::GCSlice() rather than js::GC()
      27             :  *  - the GC mode must have been set to JSGC_MODE_INCREMENTAL with
      28             :  *    JS_SetGCParameter()
      29             :  *  - no thread may have an AutoKeepAtoms instance on the stack
      30             :  *
      31             :  * The last condition is an engine-internal mechanism to ensure that incremental
      32             :  * collection is not carried out without the correct barriers being implemented.
      33             :  * For more information see 'Incremental marking' below.
      34             :  *
      35             :  * If the collection is not incremental, all foreground activity happens inside
      36             :  * a single call to GC() or GCSlice(). However the collection is not complete
      37             :  * until the background sweeping activity has finished.
      38             :  *
      39             :  * An incremental collection proceeds as a series of slices, interleaved with
      40             :  * mutator activity, i.e. running JavaScript code. Slices are limited by a time
      41             :  * budget. The slice finishes as soon as possible after the requested time has
      42             :  * passed.
      43             :  *
      44             :  * Collector states
      45             :  * ----------------
      46             :  *
      47             :  * The collector proceeds through the following states, the current state being
      48             :  * held in JSRuntime::gcIncrementalState:
      49             :  *
      50             :  *  - MarkRoots  - marks the stack and other roots
      51             :  *  - Mark       - incrementally marks reachable things
      52             :  *  - Sweep      - sweeps zones in groups and continues marking unswept zones
      53             :  *  - Finalize   - performs background finalization, concurrent with mutator
      54             :  *  - Compact    - incrementally compacts by zone
      55             :  *  - Decommit   - performs background decommit and chunk removal
      56             :  *
      57             :  * The MarkRoots activity always takes place in the first slice. The next two
      58             :  * states can take place over one or more slices.
      59             :  *
      60             :  * In other words an incremental collection proceeds like this:
      61             :  *
      62             :  * Slice 1:   MarkRoots:  Roots pushed onto the mark stack.
      63             :  *            Mark:       The mark stack is processed by popping an element,
      64             :  *                        marking it, and pushing its children.
      65             :  *
      66             :  *          ... JS code runs ...
      67             :  *
      68             :  * Slice 2:   Mark:       More mark stack processing.
      69             :  *
      70             :  *          ... JS code runs ...
      71             :  *
      72             :  * Slice n-1: Mark:       More mark stack processing.
      73             :  *
      74             :  *          ... JS code runs ...
      75             :  *
      76             :  * Slice n:   Mark:       Mark stack is completely drained.
      77             :  *            Sweep:      Select first group of zones to sweep and sweep them.
      78             :  *
      79             :  *          ... JS code runs ...
      80             :  *
      81             :  * Slice n+1: Sweep:      Mark objects in unswept zones that were newly
      82             :  *                        identified as alive (see below). Then sweep more zone
      83             :  *                        sweep groups.
      84             :  *
      85             :  *          ... JS code runs ...
      86             :  *
      87             :  * Slice n+2: Sweep:      Mark objects in unswept zones that were newly
      88             :  *                        identified as alive. Then sweep more zones.
      89             :  *
      90             :  *          ... JS code runs ...
      91             :  *
      92             :  * Slice m:   Sweep:      Sweeping is finished, and background sweeping
      93             :  *                        started on the helper thread.
      94             :  *
      95             :  *          ... JS code runs, remaining sweeping done on background thread ...
      96             :  *
      97             :  * When background sweeping finishes the GC is complete.
      98             :  *
      99             :  * Incremental marking
     100             :  * -------------------
     101             :  *
     102             :  * Incremental collection requires close collaboration with the mutator (i.e.,
     103             :  * JS code) to guarantee correctness.
     104             :  *
     105             :  *  - During an incremental GC, if a memory location (except a root) is written
     106             :  *    to, then the value it previously held must be marked. Write barriers
     107             :  *    ensure this.
     108             :  *
     109             :  *  - Any object that is allocated during incremental GC must start out marked.
     110             :  *
     111             :  *  - Roots are marked in the first slice and hence don't need write barriers.
     112             :  *    Roots are things like the C stack and the VM stack.
     113             :  *
     114             :  * The problem that write barriers solve is that between slices the mutator can
     115             :  * change the object graph. We must ensure that it cannot do this in such a way
     116             :  * that makes us fail to mark a reachable object (marking an unreachable object
     117             :  * is tolerable).
     118             :  *
     119             :  * We use a snapshot-at-the-beginning algorithm to do this. This means that we
     120             :  * promise to mark at least everything that is reachable at the beginning of
     121             :  * collection. To implement it we mark the old contents of every non-root memory
     122             :  * location written to by the mutator while the collection is in progress, using
     123             :  * write barriers. This is described in gc/Barrier.h.
     124             :  *
     125             :  * Incremental sweeping
     126             :  * --------------------
     127             :  *
     128             :  * Sweeping is difficult to do incrementally because object finalizers must be
     129             :  * run at the start of sweeping, before any mutator code runs. The reason is
     130             :  * that some objects use their finalizers to remove themselves from caches. If
     131             :  * mutator code was allowed to run after the start of sweeping, it could observe
     132             :  * the state of the cache and create a new reference to an object that was just
     133             :  * about to be destroyed.
     134             :  *
     135             :  * Sweeping all finalizable objects in one go would introduce long pauses, so
     136             :  * instead sweeping broken up into groups of zones. Zones which are not yet
     137             :  * being swept are still marked, so the issue above does not apply.
     138             :  *
     139             :  * The order of sweeping is restricted by cross compartment pointers - for
     140             :  * example say that object |a| from zone A points to object |b| in zone B and
     141             :  * neither object was marked when we transitioned to the Sweep phase. Imagine we
     142             :  * sweep B first and then return to the mutator. It's possible that the mutator
     143             :  * could cause |a| to become alive through a read barrier (perhaps it was a
     144             :  * shape that was accessed via a shape table). Then we would need to mark |b|,
     145             :  * which |a| points to, but |b| has already been swept.
     146             :  *
     147             :  * So if there is such a pointer then marking of zone B must not finish before
     148             :  * marking of zone A.  Pointers which form a cycle between zones therefore
     149             :  * restrict those zones to being swept at the same time, and these are found
     150             :  * using Tarjan's algorithm for finding the strongly connected components of a
     151             :  * graph.
     152             :  *
     153             :  * GC things without finalizers, and things with finalizers that are able to run
     154             :  * in the background, are swept on the background thread. This accounts for most
     155             :  * of the sweeping work.
     156             :  *
     157             :  * Reset
     158             :  * -----
     159             :  *
     160             :  * During incremental collection it is possible, although unlikely, for
     161             :  * conditions to change such that incremental collection is no longer safe. In
     162             :  * this case, the collection is 'reset' by ResetIncrementalGC(). If we are in
     163             :  * the mark state, this just stops marking, but if we have started sweeping
     164             :  * already, we continue until we have swept the current sweep group. Following a
     165             :  * reset, a new non-incremental collection is started.
     166             :  *
     167             :  * Compacting GC
     168             :  * -------------
     169             :  *
     170             :  * Compacting GC happens at the end of a major GC as part of the last slice.
     171             :  * There are three parts:
     172             :  *
     173             :  *  - Arenas are selected for compaction.
     174             :  *  - The contents of those arenas are moved to new arenas.
     175             :  *  - All references to moved things are updated.
     176             :  *
     177             :  * Collecting Atoms
     178             :  * ----------------
     179             :  *
     180             :  * Atoms are collected differently from other GC things. They are contained in
     181             :  * a special zone and things in other zones may have pointers to them that are
     182             :  * not recorded in the cross compartment pointer map. Each zone holds a bitmap
     183             :  * with the atoms it might be keeping alive, and atoms are only collected if
     184             :  * they are not included in any zone's atom bitmap. See AtomMarking.cpp for how
     185             :  * this bitmap is managed.
     186             :  */
     187             :

     397             : 
     398             : // Incremental sweeping is controlled by a list of actions that describe what
     399             : // happens and in what order. Due to the incremental nature of sweeping an
     400             : // action does not necessarily run to completion so the current state is tracked
     401             : // in the GCRuntime by the performSweepActions() method.
     402             : //
     403             : // Actions are performed in phases run per sweep group, and each action is run
     404             : // for every zone in the group, i.e. as if by the following pseudocode:
     405             : //
     406             : //   for each sweep group:
     407             : //     for each phase:
     408             : //       for each zone in sweep group:
     409             : //         for each action in phase:
     410             : //           perform_action
     411             : 
     412             : struct SweepAction
     413             : {
     414             :     using Func = IncrementalProgress (*)(GCRuntime* gc, FreeOp* fop, Zone* zone,
     415             :                                          SliceBudget& budget, AllocKind kind);
     416             : 
     417             :     Func func;
     418             :     AllocKind kind;
     419             : 
     420           1 :     SweepAction(Func func, AllocKind kind) : func(func), kind(kind) {}
     421             : };
     422             : 
     423             : using SweepActionVector = Vector<SweepAction, 0, SystemAllocPolicy>;
     424             : using SweepPhaseVector = Vector<SweepActionVector, 0, SystemAllocPolicy>;
     425             : 
     426           1 : static SweepPhaseVector SweepPhases;
     427             : 
     428             : bool
     429           1 : js::gc::InitializeStaticData()
     430             : {
     431           1 :     return GCRuntime::initializeSweepActions();
     432             : }
     433             : 
     434             : template<>
     435             : JSObject*

     438             :     MOZ_ASSERT(!done());

     511             :     }
     512             :

     514             :         // Do nothing. The caller will update the arena appropriately.
     515             :         MOZ_ASSERT(newListTail == &newListHead);
     516             :         JS_EXTRA_POISON(data, JS_SWEPT_TENURED_PATTERN, sizeof(data));
     517             :         return nmarked;

    2449             : 
    2450             : // After cells have been relocated any pointers to a cell's old locations must
    2451             : // be updated to point to the new location.  This happens by iterating through
    2452             : // all cells in heap and tracing their children (non-recursively) to update
    2453             : // them.
    2454             : //
    2455             : // This is complicated by the fact that updating a GC thing sometimes depends on
    2456             : // making use of other GC things.  After a moving GC these things may not be in
    2457             : // a valid state since they may contain pointers which have not been updated
    2458             : // yet.
    2459             : //
    2460             : // The main dependencies are:
    2461             : //
    2462             : //   - Updating a JSObject makes use of its shape
    2463             : //   - Updating a typed object makes use of its type descriptor object
    2464             : //
    2465             : // This means we require at least three phases for update:
    2466             : //
    2467             : //  1) shapes
    2468             : //  2) typed object type descriptor objects
    2469             : //  3) all other objects
    2470             : //
    2471             : // Since we want to minimize the number of phases, we put everything else into
    2472             : // the first phase and label it the 'misc' phase.
    2473             :

    4000             : void
    4001           1 : GCRuntime::markCompartments()
    4002             : {
    4003           1 :     gcstats::AutoPhase ap(stats(), gcstats::PHASE_MARK_COMPARTMENTS);
    4004             : 
    4005             :     /*
    4006             :      * This code ensures that if a compartment is "dead", then it will be
    4007             :      * collected in this GC. A compartment is considered dead if its maybeAlive
    4008             :      * flag is false. The maybeAlive flag is set if:
    4009             :      *
    4010             :      *   (1) the compartment has been entered (set in beginMarkPhase() above)
    4011             :      *   (2) the compartment is not being collected (set in beginMarkPhase()
    4012             :      *       above)
    4013             :      *   (3) an object in the compartment was marked during root marking, either
    4014             :      *       as a black root or a gray root (set in RootMarking.cpp), or
    4015             :      *   (4) the compartment has incoming cross-compartment edges from another
    4016             :      *       compartment that has maybeAlive set (set by this method).
    4017             :      *
    4018             :      * If the maybeAlive is false, then we set the scheduledForDestruction flag.
    4019             :      * At the end of the GC, we look for compartments where
    4020             :      * scheduledForDestruction is true. These are compartments that were somehow
    4021             :      * "revived" during the incremental GC. If any are found, we do a special,
    4022             :      * non-incremental GC of those compartments to try to collect them.
    4023             :      *
    4024             :      * Compartments can be revived for a variety of reasons. On reason is bug
    4025             :      * 811587, where a reflector that was dead can be revived by DOM code that
    4026             :      * still refers to the underlying DOM node.
    4027             :      *
    4028             :      * Read barriers and allocations can also cause revival. This might happen
    4029             :      * during a function like JS_TransplantObject, which iterates over all
    4030             :      * compartments, live or dead, and operates on their objects. See bug 803376
    4031             :      * for details on this problem. To avoid the problem, we try to avoid
    4032             :      * allocation and read barriers during JS_TransplantObject and the like.
    4033             :      */
    4034             : 
    4035             :     /* Propagate the maybeAlive flag via cross-compartment edges. */
    4036             : 
    4037             :     Vector<JSCompartment*, 0, js::SystemAllocPolicy> workList;
    4038             :

    4041           1 :             if (!workList.append(comp))
    4042           0 :                 return;
    4043             :         }
    4044           1 :     }
    4045             :

    4451             : 
    4452             : /*
    4453             :  * Group zones that must be swept at the same time.
    4454             :  *
    4455             :  * If compartment A has an edge to an unmarked object in compartment B, then we
    4456             :  * must not sweep A in a later slice than we sweep B. That's because a write
    4457             :  * barrier in A could lead to the unmarked object in B becoming marked.
    4458             :  * However, if we had already swept that object, we would be in trouble.
    4459             :  *

    4461             :  * any strongly-connected component of this graph must be swept in the same
    4462             :  * slice.
    4463             :  *
    4464             :  * Tarjan's algorithm is used to calculate the components.

    4665             : 
    4666             : /*
    4667             :  * Gray marking:
    4668             :  *
    4669             :  * At the end of collection, anything reachable from a gray root that has not
    4670             :  * otherwise been marked black must be marked gray.
    4671             :  *
    4672             :  * This means that when marking things gray we must not allow marking to leave
    4673             :  * the current compartment group, as that could result in things being marked
    4674             :  * grey when they might subsequently be marked black.  To achieve this, when we
    4675             :  * find a cross compartment pointer we don't mark the referent but add it to a
    4676             :  * singly-linked list of incoming gray pointers that is stored with each
    4677             :  * compartment.
    4678             :  *
    4679             :  * The list head is stored in JSCompartment::gcIncomingGrayPointers and contains
    4680             :  * cross compartment wrapper objects. The next pointer is stored in the second
    4681             :  * extra slot of the cross compartment wrapper.
    4682             :  *
    4683             :  * The list is created during gray marking when one of the
    4684             :  * MarkCrossCompartmentXXX functions is called for a pointer that leaves the
    4685             :  * current compartent group.  This calls DelayCrossCompartmentGrayMarking to
    4686             :  * push the referring object onto the list.
    4687             :  *
    4688             :  * The list is traversed and then unlinked in
    4689             :  * MarkIncomingCrossCompartmentPointers.
    4690             :  */
    4691             :

    6387             : /*
    6388             :  * An invariant of our GC/CC interaction is that there must not ever be any
    6389             :  * black to gray edges in the system. It is possible to violate this with
    6390             :  * simple compartmental GC. For example, in GC[n], we collect in both
    6391             :  * compartmentA and compartmentB, and mark both sides of the cross-compartment
    6392             :  * edge gray. Later in GC[n+1], we only collect compartmentA, but this time
    6393             :  * mark it black. Now we are violating the invariants and must fix it somehow.
    6394             :  *
    6395             :  * To prevent this situation, we explicitly detect the black->gray state when
    6396             :  * marking cross-compartment edges -- see ShouldMarkCrossCompartment -- adding
    6397             :  * each violating edges to foundBlackGrayEdges. After we leave the trace
    6398             :  * session for each GC slice, we "ExposeToActiveJS" on each of these edges

    8018           1 : js::gc::detail::CellIsMarkedGrayIfKnown(const Cell* cell)
    8019             : {
    8020             :     // We ignore the gray marking state of cells and return false in the
    8021             :     // following cases:
    8022             :     //
    8023             :     // 1) When OOM has caused us to clear the gcGrayBitsValid_ flag.
    8024             :     //
    8025             :     // 2) When we are in an incremental GC and examine a cell that is in a zone
    8026             :     // that is not being collected. Gray targets of CCWs that are marked black
    8027             :     // by a barrier will eventually be marked black in the next GC slice.
    8028             :     //
    8029             :     // 3) When we are not on the runtime's active thread. Helper threads might
    8030             :     // call this while parsing, and they are not allowed to inspect the
    8031             :     // runtime's incremental state. The objects being operated on are not able
    8032             :     // to be collected and will not be marked any color.
    8033             : 
    8034           1 :     if (!CanCheckGrayBits(cell))
    8035             :         return false;
